Angels and the Celestial Hierarchy
Razi describes celestial structures and argues angelic superiority by analogy with physical domination.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Razi uses the structure of the cosmos—spheres, planets, and stars—to argue for the superiority of angels over humans.

Core Idea
The cosmos is a hierarchy: upper structures dominate lower, so upper spirits dominate lower spirits.

Imam Razi presents his twenty-second argument for the superiority of angels by examining the celestial order. He describes the noble structures (planets and fixed stars) as the bodies of the spiritual realm, with angels as their spirits. By observing how celestial motions affect the lower world, he establishes a clear hierarchy that extends from physical structures to spiritual beings.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyze it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that Razi uses a layered description: spheres, stars, then spirits.
2
Identify the cosmic components
Find the description of the noble structures (planets, fixed stars), spheres as bodies, stars as hearts, and angels as spirits. Note the hierarchy.
This sets up the analogy for spiritual hierarchy.
3
Understand ratq and fatq
Razi introduces the concepts of closure (ratq) and opening (fatq) of the spheres' zones. Observe how these cause changes in the lower world—cessation or transfer of flourishing.
This demonstrates the influence of upper structures on the lower world.
4
Follow the analogy to spirits
Since upper structures dominate lower structures, Razi concludes that upper spirits must dominate lower spirits. Consider the logical step from physical hierarchy to spiritual hierarchy.
This is the core of the argument for angelic superiority.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الثانية والعشرون: الروحانيون مختصون بالهياكل الشريفة - وهي السيارات السبع وسائر الثوابت - والأفلاك لها كالأبدان والكواكب كالقلوب، والملائكة كالأرواح، ونسبة الأرواح إلى الأرواح كنسبة الأبدان إلى الأبدان، ثم إنا نعلم أن اختلاف أحوال الكواكب والأفلاك يتأدى لحصول الاختلافات في أحوال هذا العالم، فإنه يحصل من حركات الكواكب مناطق الأفلاك تارة ينطبق بعضها على بعض - وهو الرتق - وعنده تبطل عمارة العالم، وأخرى ينفصل بعضها عن بعض - وذلك هو الفتق - وعنده تنتقل العمارة في هذا العالم السفلي من جانب إلى جنب. فإذا رأينا أن هياكل العالم العلوي مسئولية على هياكل العالم السفلي فكذا أرواح العالم العلوي يجب أن تكون مستولية على أرواح العالم السفلي، لاسيما وقد دلت المباحث الفلسفية على أن أرواح هذا العالم معلولات أرواح العالم العلوي، ونسبة كمالات هذا العالم معلولات لكمال ذلك العالم، وكمالات هذه الأرواح إلى أرواح ذلك العالم وكمالاته كالشعلة الصغيرة بالنسبة إلى قرص الشمس، وكالقطرة الصغيرة في البحر الأعظم. وهذه الأرواح البشرية كالذرات وأما البحار والعيون والجبال والمعادن، فهي كالأرواح العلوية، فكيف يمكن أن يقابل أحدهما بالآخر ؟ فهذاه حكاية أدلة الفريقين في هذه المسألة على الاختصار.
The twenty-second argument: The spiritual beings are specialized with noble structures—that is the seven planets and the rest of the fixed stars—and the spheres are like bodies for them, and the stars are like hearts, and the angels are like spirits. And the relation of spirits to spirits is like the relation of bodies to bodies. Then we know that the differing states of the stars and spheres lead to differences in the states of this world, for from the movements of the stars the zones of the spheres sometimes overlap each other—that is closure (ratq)—and at that time the flourishing of the world ceases, and other times they separate from each other—that is opening (fatq)—and at that time flourishing transfers in this lower world from one side to another. So if we see that the structures of the upper world are dominant over the structures of the lower world, likewise the spirits of the upper world must be dominant over the spirits of the lower world, especially since philosophical investigations have shown that the spirits of this world are effects of the spirits of the upper world, and the relation of the perfections of this world is that they are effects of the perfections of that world, and the perfections of these spirits compared to the spirits of that world and its perfections are like a small flame compared to the disc of the sun, and like a small drop in the great ocean. And these human spirits are like atoms, while the seas, springs, mountains, and minerals are like the upper spirits. So how can one be compared to the other? This is the account of the proofs of the two groups on this issue in summary.
Source pages p. 372

Commentary
This passage presents the twenty-second argument for the superiority of angels. It is an argument from cosmic hierarchy and causation. Imam Razi begins by describing the structure of the celestial realm: angels are associated with noble structures—the seven planets and fixed stars. The spheres are like bodies, the stars like hearts, and the angels like spirits. The relationship between upper and lower spirits mirrors that between upper and lower bodies. He then introduces the astronomical concepts of ratq (closure) and fatq (opening), where the overlapping or separation of celestial spheres causes changes in the lower world—cessation or transfer of flourishing. Since the upper structures dominate the lower, so too must the upper spirits dominate the lower spirits. Philosophical investigations confirm that lower spirits are effects (ma'lulat) of upper spirits, and the perfections of the lower world depend on the perfections of the upper world. The disparity is likened to a small flame versus the sun, or a drop versus the ocean. Human spirits are compared to atoms, while upper spirits are like seas, mountains, etc. The argument concludes that the two are incomparable. This argument synthesizes cosmological observation with philosophical causation to establish a clear hierarchy.

Key Terms
الهياكل الشريفة
السيارات السبع
الرتق والفتق
الأرواح العلوية والسفلية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think the argument is purely philosophical and not grounded in observation.
Correction: Razi relies on observable celestial motions (ratq and fatq) and scriptural references to angels' roles, combining philosophy and cosmology.

Checkpoint
What do the terms 'ratq' and 'fatq' refer to in this argument?
A) The creation and destruction of stars
B) The overlapping and separation of celestial spheres
C) The birth and death of angels
D) The movement of planets around the sun

Key Takeaway
The physical hierarchy of the cosmos mirrors and justifies the spiritual hierarchy, with angels at the top.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If the angels are as superior to you as the sun to a flame, how does this reshape your daily awareness of your own limitations and dependence on Allah's mercy? Will you today consciously remind yourself of your lowly status and seek refuge from arrogance?
?
Razi argues that your spirit is like an atom compared to the vastness of the upper spirits. How does this humble your ambitions when you strive for status or recognition? What one concrete action will you take today to lower yourself in humility before the unseen realities?
?
The hierarchy of spirits is mirrored in the physical world. If you truly believed that your deeds are witnessed by beings far superior, how would that change your private moments? Commit to one small act of obedience that only you and Allah (and His angels) know about.

The Causation and Analogy of Spiritual Perfection
Razi presents causal proofs and analogies for angelic superiority.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Razi uses philosophical causation and vivid analogies to prove that angels' perfections far surpass human perfections.

Core Idea
Lower spirits are mere effects of upper spirits; their perfections are like a spark compared to the sun.

After establishing the physical hierarchy, Imam Razi deepens the argument with philosophical reasoning. He states that lower spirits are effects (ma'lulat) of upper spirits and that all perfections of the lower world derive from the upper. He employs striking analogies—a small flame versus the sun, a drop versus the ocean, atoms versus seas—to demonstrate the incomparable superiority of angelic spirits over human spirits.

Guided Path
1
Locate the causal claim
Find where Razi states that lower spirits are effects (ma'lulat) of upper spirits. This is a key philosophical premise.
The phrase 'معلولات أرواح العالم العلوي' indicates causation.
2
Understand the chain of perfections
Razi says the perfections of this world are effects of the perfections of the upper world. Consider how this establishes a dependent relationship.
Implication: lower perfections are derived and limited.
3
Analyze the analogies
Razi uses three analogies: a small flame to the sun, a small drop to the ocean, and human spirits as atoms to upper spirits as vast elements. Compare the scale.
The analogies emphasize vast disparity, not just difference.
4
Grasp the conclusion
The final rhetorical question 'how can one be compared to the other?' underscores the incomparability. Understand that this concludes the argument for angelic superiority.
The conclusion is that human and angelic perfections are categorically distinct.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الثانية والعشرون: الروحانيون مختصون بالهياكل الشريفة - وهي السيارات السبع وسائر الثوابت - والأفلاك لها كالأبدان والكواكب كالقلوب، والملائكة كالأرواح، ونسبة الأرواح إلى الأرواح كنسبة الأبدان إلى الأبدان، ثم إنا نعلم أن اختلاف أحوال الكواكب والأفلاك يتأدى لحصول الاختلافات في أحوال هذا العالم، فإنه يحصل من حركات الكواكب مناطق الأفلاك تارة ينطبق بعضها على بعض - وهو الرتق - وعنده تبطل عمارة العالم، وأخرى ينفصل بعضها عن بعض - وذلك هو الفتق - وعنده تنتقل العمارة في هذا العالم السفلي من جانب إلى جنب. فإذا رأينا أن هياكل العالم العلوي مسئولية على هياكل العالم السفلي فكذا أرواح العالم العلوي يجب أن تكون مستولية على أرواح العالم السفلي، لاسيما وقد دلت المباحث الفلسفية على أن أرواح هذا العالم معلولات أرواح العالم العلوي، ونسبة كمالات هذا العالم معلولات لكمال ذلك العالم، وكمالات هذه الأرواح إلى أرواح ذلك العالم وكمالاته كالشعلة الصغيرة بالنسبة إلى قرص الشمس، وكالقطرة الصغيرة في البحر الأعظم. وهذه الأرواح البشرية كالذرات وأما البحار والعيون والجبال والمعادن، فهي كالأرواح العلوية، فكيف يمكن أن يقابل أحدهما بالآخر ؟ فهذاه حكاية أدلة الفريقين في هذه المسألة على الاختصار.
The twenty-second argument: The spiritual beings are specialized with noble structures—that is the seven planets and the rest of the fixed stars—and the spheres are like bodies for them, and the stars are like hearts, and the angels are like spirits. And the relation of spirits to spirits is like the relation of bodies to bodies. Then we know that the differing states of the stars and spheres lead to differences in the states of this world, for from the movements of the stars the zones of the spheres sometimes overlap each other—that is closure (ratq)—and at that time the flourishing of the world ceases, and other times they separate from each other—that is opening (fatq)—and at that time flourishing transfers in this lower world from one side to another. So if we see that the structures of the upper world are dominant over the structures of the lower world, likewise the spirits of the upper world must be dominant over the spirits of the lower world, especially since philosophical investigations have shown that the spirits of this world are effects of the spirits of the upper world, and the relation of the perfections of this world is that they are effects of the perfections of that world, and the perfections of these spirits compared to the spirits of that world and its perfections are like a small flame compared to the disc of the sun, and like a small drop in the great ocean. And these human spirits are like atoms, while the seas, springs, mountains, and minerals are like the upper spirits. So how can one be compared to the other? This is the account of the proofs of the two groups on this issue in summary.
Source pages p. 372

Commentary
This passage presents the twenty-second argument for the superiority of angels. It is an argument from cosmic hierarchy and causation. Imam Razi begins by describing the structure of the celestial realm: angels are associated with noble structures—the seven planets and fixed stars. The spheres are like bodies, the stars like hearts, and the angels like spirits. The relationship between upper and lower spirits mirrors that between upper and lower bodies. He then introduces the astronomical concepts of ratq (closure) and fatq (opening), where the overlapping or separation of celestial spheres causes changes in the lower world—cessation or transfer of flourishing. Since the upper structures dominate the lower, so too must the upper spirits dominate the lower spirits. Philosophical investigations confirm that lower spirits are effects (ma'lulat) of upper spirits, and the perfections of the lower world depend on the perfections of the upper world. The disparity is likened to a small flame versus the sun, or a drop versus the ocean. Human spirits are compared to atoms, while upper spirits are like seas, mountains, etc. The argument concludes that the two are incomparable. This argument synthesizes cosmological observation with philosophical causation to establish a clear hierarchy.

Key Terms
الأرواح العلوية والسفلية
معلولات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think the argument is purely philosophical and not grounded in observation.
Correction: Razi relies on observable celestial motions (ratq and fatq) and scriptural references to angels' roles, combining philosophy and cosmology.

Checkpoint
What analogy does Imam Razi use to compare the perfections of human spirits to angelic spirits?
A) A small flame to the sun
B) A drop to the ocean
C) Atoms to vast elements
D) All of the above

Key Takeaway
The perfections of angels so exceed human perfections that comparison is impossible—like comparing a flame to the sun.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Razi compares your spiritual perfection to a small flame next to the sun. If you truly believed that, would you still feel proud of your spiritual achievements? What specific act of humility can you perform today to align with this reality?
?
The passage says your spirit is an effect of angelic spirits. Do you live as though you are utterly dependent on forces beyond your control, or do you act as if you are self-sufficient? What one change in your daily attitude would remind you of your place in the cosmic hierarchy?
?
The analogy of drop in the ocean is meant to show your insignificance. How does that make you feel about your sins and your worship? Are you still comfortable with sins that you think are 'small'? Will you repent of one specific sin today because you now see the immense gap between you and the angels?

First Proof for Miracles of Saints from Maryam's Story
Razi presents the first proof for saints' miracles and refutes an objection with three responses.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam al-Razi uses the story of Maryam (AS) as the first proof for the miracles of saints (karamat al-awliya) and how he refutes the objection that these events were prophetic miracles for Zakariyya (AS).

Core Idea
Maryam's miracles without prophethood prove that saints can perform miracles.

In this passage, Imam al-Razi begins the discussion on the miracles of saints by presenting his first proof. He draws from the well-known story of Maryam, who experienced extraordinary events—pregnancy without a male and provision without apparent cause—despite not being a prophet. After establishing that these are violations of custom, he anticipates and refutes an objection that these might have been miracles for the prophet of the time, Zakariyya. Through three logical arguments, he demonstrates why that objection is invalid, thereby supporting the Ash'ari position that saints can indeed perform miracles.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage and the literal translation to get an overall sense of the argument.
Focus on the flow from the proof to the objection and the three responses.
2
Identify the core proof
Notice how Razi uses the two violations of custom in Maryam's life and the fact that she was not a prophet to argue for saintly miracles.
What makes this proof effective?
3
Analyze the objection and the three refutations
The objection suggests these events were miracles for Zakariyya. Razi gives three reasons why this is false. Read each one and understand the logic.
Pay attention to the conditions of a prophetic miracle that Razi lists.
4
Reflect on the significance
Consider how this argument supports the broader Ash'ari doctrine of karamat al-awliya and counters the Mu'tazila denial.
This is one of three proofs Razi will present.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المسألة الرابعة والثلاثون
في كرامات الأولياء
المعتزلة ينكرونها، ووافقهم الأستاذ أبو إسحاق من أصحابنا، وأكثر أصحابنا يثبتونها، وبه قال أبو الحسين البصري من المعتزلة.
لنا
وجوه ثلاثة :
الحجة الأولى : أن حدوث الحبل لمريم من غير الذكر من خوارق العادات، وحضور الرزق عندها من غير سبب ظاهر ومن خوارق العادات وأنها ما كانت من الأنبياء، فوجب أن يقال : إن هذه الوقائع من كرامات الأولياء.
فإن قيل : لم لا يجوز أن يقال: إن تلك الخوارق كانت معجزات لنبي ذلك الزمان، وهو زكريا ?
قلنا : هذا باطل لوجوه.
الأول : أن المعجزة لا بد أن تكون أمرًا ظاهرًا للمنكرين حتى يمكن الاستدلال بها على المنكر، وظهور جبريل لمريم وحبلها من غير ذكر، ما كان يطلع عليه أحد إلا مريم فكيف يمكن جعل هذه الأشياء معجزة لزكريا ؟
ثانيها : أن عند ظهور المعجز لبعض الأنبياء لا بد أن يكون الرسول حاضرًا، ولا بد أن يكون القوم حاضرين حتى يتمكن ذلك الرسول من الاستدلال بذلك المعجز، وفي الوقت الذي كان يقول جبريل لمريم : ﴿وَهُزَى إِلَيْكِ يجذع النَّخْلَةِ تسقط عليك رطباً جنتا﴾ [مريم : ٢٥] من كان زكريا حاضرًا هناك حتى يستدل بظهور هذه الخوارق على نبوة نفسه بل ما كان أحد من البشر هناك حاضراً، بدليل قوله تعالى: ﴿فَإِمَّا تَرَينَ مِنَ الْبَشَرِ أَحَدًا فَقُولِي إِنِّي نَذَرْتُ لِلرَّحْمَنِ صَوْمَال﴾ [مريم : ٢٦] فبطل القول بأن هذه الأشياء معجزة لزكريا .
ثالثها: أن حصول المعجز لا بد أن يكون بالتماس الرسول، وكان زكريا غافلا عن كيفية حدوث هذه الأشياء، بدليل قوله تعالى : ﴿كُلَّمَا دَخَلَ عَلَيْهَا زَكَرِيَّا﴾ [آل عمران: ٣٧] ...
The Thirty-Fourth Issue: On the Miracles of Saints. The Mu'tazila deny them, and al-Ustadh Abu Ishaq among our companions agreed with them. Most of our companions affirm them, and Abu al-Husayn al-Basri of the Mu'tazila also said so. We have three proofs: The first proof: That the occurrence of pregnancy for Maryam without a male is a violation of custom, and the provision coming to her without an apparent cause is a violation of custom, and she was not among the prophets. Therefore, it must be said that these events are among the miracles of saints. If it is said: Why is it not permissible to say that those violations were miracles for the prophet of that time, namely Zakariyya? We say: This is false for reasons. First: A miracle must be a matter manifest to the deniers so that it can be used as evidence against the denier. The appearance of Jibril to Maryam and her pregnancy without a male were not witnessed by anyone except Maryam. So how can these things be made a miracle for Zakariyya? Second: When a miracle appears for a certain prophet, the messenger must be present, and the people must be present so that that messenger can use that miracle as evidence. At the time when Jibril said to Maryam: 'And shake toward yourself the trunk of the palm tree; it will drop upon you fresh, ripe dates' [Maryam:25], was Zakariyya present there to use the appearance of these violations as evidence for his own prophethood? Rather, there was no human being present there, as evidenced by His saying: 'So if you see any human, say: Indeed, I have vowed to the Most Merciful a fast' [Maryam:26]. So the claim that these things are miracles for Zakariyya is invalid. Third: The occurrence of a miracle must be at the request of the messenger, and Zakariyya was unaware of how these things happened, as evidenced by His saying: 'Every time Zakariyya entered upon her in the sanctuary' [Aal-Imran:37]...
Source pages p. 374

Commentary
This passage opens the Thirty-Fourth Issue on the miracles of saints (karamat al-awliya). Razi first states the positions: the Mu'tazila deny them, and among the Ash'aris, Abu Ishaq al-Isfarayini agreed with them, but the majority of Ash'aris affirm them, and even the Mu'tazilite Abu al-Husayn al-Basri affirmed them. Then Razi presents three proofs. The first proof is based on the story of Maryam. Maryam experienced two violations of custom (khawariq al-'adat): becoming pregnant without a male, and receiving provision without an apparent cause. Maryam was not a prophet, so if these violations are not considered prophetic miracles, they must be considered saintly miracles. Razi then anticipates an objection: could these not be miracles for the prophet of the time, Zakariyya? He refutes this with three points. First, a miracle must be manifest to deniers; but Maryam's experiences were private, known only to her. Second, a miracle requires the prophet and his audience to be present so the prophet can use it as evidence; but when Jibril came to Maryam and she gave birth, no one else was present, as the Quran indicates by commanding her to say she vowed a fast if she sees any human. Third, a miracle must be at the prophet's request; Zakariyya was unaware of these events, as the Quran shows him entering her sanctuary and finding provision, not requesting it. The text ends mid-sentence in the third refutation.

Key Terms
كرامات الأولياء
معجزات
خوارق العادات
المعتزلة
أبو إسحاق
مريم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think that any violation of custom must be a prophetic miracle.
Correction: Razi shows that it can be a saintly miracle if the person is not a prophet, as in the case of Maryam.

Checkpoint
Why does Razi present the story of Maryam as evidence for the miracles of saints?
A) Because Maryam was a prophet and her miracles prove prophecy.
B) Because Maryam experienced violations of custom despite not being a prophet.
C) Because Maryam's miracles were witnessed by many people.
D) Because Maryam was a companion of Zakariyya.

Key Takeaway
Maryam's story provides a clear example of saintly miracles, as she experienced violations of custom without being a prophet, and these cannot be attributed to Zakariyya for three reasons.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read that Maryam's miracles were private—known only to her—does it challenge your need for public recognition in your own acts of devotion? Are you willing to serve Allah even if no one ever sees your sacrifice?
?
Razi argues that a miracle must be manifest to deniers to serve as evidence. In your own life, are you more concerned with appearing righteous to others (deniers or not) than with the hidden reality of your faith that only Allah sees?
?
If Maryam, a non-prophet, could experience such profound interventions from Allah, what does that say about your own potential for divine closeness? Are you living as if you expect Allah to support you in extraordinary ways, or have you settled for a mundane faith?

The Ash'ari Position on Reward and the First Proof
Al-Razi states the Ash'ari view and gives the first proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Ash'ari argument that no one has a right over God and the first proof based on the obligation of gratitude.

Core Idea
Past blessings obligate obedience; fulfilling an obligation cannot create a new right.

Al-Razi introduces the Ash'ari stance on reward by contrasting it with the Mu'tazili view. The first proof rests on a logical point: if God's blessings already obligate gratitude and obedience, then performing that obedience cannot be a cause for deserving additional reward. This lesson unpacks that argument.

Guided Path
1
Understand the context
The passage is from the Thirty-Fifth Issue on reward and punishment. Al-Razi first states the basic ruling: obedient people are rewarded by Allah. Then he contrasts the Mu'tazili claim that obedience is a cause for deserving reward with the Ash'ari view that no one has a right over God.
2
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic passage carefully. Note key terms: ثواب, عقاب, طاعة, استحقاق, حق, إنعام, شكر.
3
Analyze the first proof
Focus on the logic: Allah's past blessings obligate the servant to obedience and gratitude. Since performing an obligation cannot be a cause for something else, obedience cannot be a cause for deserving reward.
The proof uses the Quranic verse from Ibrahim 14:34.
4
Contrast with Mu'tazili view
Understand why the Mu'tazili view is problematic according to Ash'aris: it implies that humans have a claim on God, which is denied.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المسألة الخامسة والثلاثون وفيها فصول : في أحكام الثواب والعقاب الفصل الأول : في حكم الثواب والعقاب اعلم أن المكلف إما أن يكون مطيعا أو عاصيًا، فإن كان مطيعا فالله تعالى يثيبه، وزعم البصريون من المعتزلة أن أداء الطاعة علة لاستحقاق الثواب على الله تعالى. ومذهبنا أنه ليس لأحد على الله تعالى حق لنا وجوه : · الحجة الأولى : أن الإنعام يوجب على المنعم عليه الاشتغال بالشكر والخدمة، ونعم الله تعالى على العبد في الماضي وفي الحاضر كثيرة خارجة عن الحصر والإحصاء، كما قال تعالى: ﴿ وَإِن تَعُدُّوا نِعْمَتَ اللَّهِ لَا تُحْصُوهَا ﴾ [إبراهيم: ٣٤] وإذا كان كذلك فتلك النعم السالفة توجب على العبد الاشتغال بالطاعة وبالشكر، وأداء الواجب لا يكون سببًا لاستحقاق شيء آخر، فوجب أن لا يكون اشتغال العبد بالطاعة سببًا لاستحقاق الثواب على الله تعالى.
The Thirty-Fifth Issue, comprising chapters on the rulings of reward and punishment. Chapter One: On the ruling of reward and punishment. Know that the legally responsible person is either obedient or disobedient. If he is obedient, then Allah Most High rewards him. The Basran Mu'tazilites claimed that performing obedience is a cause for deserving reward from Allah Most High. Our school is that no one has a right over Allah Most High. For us there are proofs: The first proof: That bestowal of blessings obligates the recipient to engage in gratitude and service, and the blessings of Allah Most High upon the servant in the past and present are many, beyond enumeration and counting, as He said: 'And if you count the blessings of Allah, you cannot enumerate them.' [Ibrahim: 34]. If that is so, then those past blessings obligate the servant to engage in obedience and gratitude, and performing an obligation is not a cause for deserving something else. Therefore, the servant's engagement in obedience should not be a cause for deserving reward from Allah Most High.
Source pages p. 378

Commentary
This passage introduces the Thirty-Fifth Issue on reward and punishment, specifically the first chapter on the ruling of reward. Al-Razi begins by stating that the morally responsible person is either obedient or disobedient; if obedient, Allah rewards him. He then contrasts the Mu'tazili view (Basran school) that performing obedience is a cause ('illah) for deserving (istihqāq) reward from Allah, with the Ash'ari position that no one has a right (haqq) over Allah. The first proof (al-ḥujjah al-ūlā) argues that Allah's past and present blessings obligate the servant to gratitude and obedience, not to deserve further reward. Since the servant already owes obedience for previous blessings, fulfilling that duty cannot create a new entitlement. Thus, obedience is not a cause for deserving reward from Allah.

Key Terms
ثواب
عقاب
طاعة
معصية
استحقاق
حق
إنعام
شكر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that God is obligated to reward the obedient because obedience is good and deserves reward.
Correction: Ash'aris argue that God is not obligated by anyone's actions; rather, past blessings already obligate us, so obedience cannot be a cause for deserving reward.

Checkpoint
What is the foundation of al-Razi's first proof against the Mu'tazili view on reward?
A) That obedience cannot be a cause for reward because reward is a gift, not an obligation.
B) That Allah's past blessings already obligate obedience, so performing obedience does not create a new right to reward.
C) That the Mu'tazili view implies injustice on God's part.
D) That the Quran states reward is only in the afterlife.

Key Takeaway
The first Ash'ari proof for reward not being obligatory on God is that past blessings already obligate obedience, so performing obedience cannot create a new right to reward.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you perform acts of worship, do you ever feel that God owes you something in return? How does this lesson challenge that feeling, and what would it mean to truly let go of that transactional mindset?
?
Think of the countless blessings you have received from God since birth. How many of them have you adequately thanked Him for? Does the realization that you are already in debt change how you view your obedience – not as earning reward, but as paying back an unpayable debt?
?
If obedience does not 'earn' you reward, then why do you obey? Does this truth free you from a transactional relationship with Allah, or does it leave you uncomfortable? What needs to change in your heart so that your obedience springs from gratitude rather than from a desire to claim something?

Second Argument: Only Deniers Enter Hell
Razi presents a Qur'anic proof that only deniers enter Hell.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Razi uses the Qur'anic dialogue of Hell's keepers to prove that only deniers of prophets enter Hell.

Core Idea
Hell's inhabitants confess: we denied the warner, so only deniers are there.

Razi now turns to a direct Qur'anic proof to show that Hell is reserved for those who reject the messengers. He cites the scene where the keepers of Hell question each incoming group, and every group replies that they denied the warner who came to them. This universal confession, Razi argues, establishes that only deniers enter Hell.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage carefully
Read the Arabic text of the verse and Razi's commentary once without translating. Notice the key words: فوج, نذير, كذبناهم.
The verse is from Surah al-Mulk.
2
Understand the logic of the argument
Razi claims that the verse states 'every group' that enters Hell says the same thing: a warner came but we denied him. If every group says this, then every person in Hell is a denier.
3
Reflect on the implication
If only deniers enter Hell, then believers—even sinful ones—do not enter Hell. This is a key point in Razi's defense of the view that major sinners among believers are not in Hell forever.
This argument addresses a specific theological dispute.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والحجة الثانية : قوله تعالى : ﴿وَكُلَّمَا أُلْقِيَ فِيهَا فَوْجٌ سَأَلَهُمْ خَزَنَتُهَا أَلَمْ يَأْتِكُمْ نَذِيرٌ قَالُوا بَلَى قَدْ جَاءَنَا نَذِيرٌ فَكَذَّبْنَا وَقُلْنَا مَا نَزَّلَ اللَّهُ مِنْ شَيْءٍ﴾ [الملك: 8-9] أخبر الله تعالى أن كل فوج يدخل النار فإنهم يقولون : قد جاءنا نذير ولكن كذبناه وهذا صريح في أن كل من دخل النار كان مكذبًا بأنبياء الله تعالى، فيقتضي أن من لم يكن كذلك لم يدخل النار.
And the second proof: His saying, the Most High: 'And whenever a group is thrown into it, its keepers ask them, 'Did no warner come to you?' They say, 'Yes, a warner came to us, but we denied and said, 'Allah has not sent down anything.'' [al-Mulk 67:8-9] Allah the Most High informed that every group that enters Hell, they say: 'A warner came to us but we denied him.' This is explicit that everyone who entered Hell was a denier of the prophets of Allah, and it implies that whoever was not like that did not enter Hell.
Source pages p. 380

Commentary
This passage presents a Qur'anic argument proving that Hell-fire is exclusively for those who deny the prophets. Razi cites the verse where the keepers of Hell ask every incoming group: 'Did no warner come to you?' and they reply that a warner came but they denied him. Razi points out that this dialogue is described for every group entering Hell, which shows that every inhabitant of Hell is a denier (mukadhdhib) of Allah's prophets. Therefore, anyone who is not a denier – i.e., a believer, even if sinful – cannot enter Hell. The argument hinges on the universality of the statement: all who enter Hell confess to having denied the warner.

Key Terms
الحجة
النار
التكذيب
الأنبياء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think this verse only refers to a specific group of disbelievers, not all people in Hell.
Correction: Razi uses the general wording 'every group' (كل فوج) to show it applies universally to all who enter Hell.

Checkpoint
According to this argument, what do all who enter Hell admit?
A) They were believers but sinned
B) A warner came but they denied him
C) They never received a warner
D) They repented before death

Key Takeaway
The Qur'anic testimony of every group entering Hell confirms that only deniers of prophets enter Hell.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
In your daily life, do you ever find yourself denying Allah's warnings through your actions? When was the last time you ignored a clear sign from Allah, treating it as if it were not from Him? What will you do this week to heed a warning you have been ignoring?
?
The people of Hell confessed that a warner came to them but they denied him. Is there a truth about Islam that you have heard repeatedly but still resist applying? If you were asked by the keepers of Hell today, could you honestly say you did not receive a warner?
?
Only deniers enter Hell. This means that as long as you have faith (iman), you are not among them. But does your faith make you feel secure? Or does it drive you to obey Allah more urgently? What is one area where your actions do not match your belief that you will change today?

Third Argument: The Blazing Fire Is for Deniers
Razi argues from Quran 92:14-16 that the blazing fire is only for deniers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Razi uses the attribute of 'blazing' to generalize a Quranic verse about a specific fire to all hellfires, thereby excluding sinful believers from eternal punishment.

Core Idea
The blazing fire is for deniers only, not for sinful believers.

Imam Razi continues his proofs for the fate of sinners by citing a Quranic verse that describes a blazing fire reserved for the most wretched. However, he anticipates an objection: perhaps this verse refers only to a particular fire, not to all hellfires. In this lesson, we will see how Razi responds by focusing on the attribute of 'blazing' to argue that all hellfires share this quality, and thus the verse applies universally to disbelievers.

Guided Path
1
Read the Quranic verse and its translation
Start by reading the verse (92:14-16) in Arabic and English. Notice the terms 'blazing fire' and 'most wretched' that Razi uses as his proof.
The verse explicitly links the fire to denial and turning away.
2
Identify the objection Razi addresses
Razi presents an objection: perhaps the verse only refers to a specific fire, not all hellfires. Understand why this objection could undermine the argument.
If true, the verse would not apply to all disbelievers.
3
Analyze Razi's response
Razi argues that all hellfires are blazing, and the verse indicates that the blazing fire afflicts disbelievers. See how he extends the ruling to all hellfires.
He uses the attribute 'blazing' as a common property.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
The desired conclusion is that only deniers enter any blazing fire, so sinful believers are excluded. Confirm how this supports Razi's broader theology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والحجة الثالثة : قوله تعالى: ﴿فَأَنذَرْتُكُمْ نَارًا تَلَظَّى لَا يَصْلَاهَا إِلَّا الْأَشْقَى الَّذِي كَذَّبَ وَتَوَلَّى﴾ [الليل: 14-16] ولا يقال : قوله تعالى : فأَنذرتكم نارا تلفى [الليل: 14] نار مخصوصة، وهي مختصة بالأشقى الَّذِى كَذَّبَ وَتَوَلَّى [الليل: 16] فلم قلتم : إن سائر النيران لا يدخلها فساق أهل الصلاة؟ لأنا نقول : النيران لا بد أن تكون متلظية والآية دلت على أن النار المتلظية تصيب الكفار، وحينئذ يحصل المطلوب.
And the third proof: His saying, the Most High: 'So I have warned you of a blazing fire. None shall enter it except the most wretched, who denies and turns away.' [al-Layl 92:14-16] And it is not said: His saying 'I have warned you of a fire' [al-Layl 92:14] refers to a specific fire, which is specific to the most wretched who denies and turns away [al-Layl 92:16] – so why do you say that other fires do not enter them the sinful among the people of prayer? For we say: All fires must be blazing, and the verse indicates that the blazing fire afflicts the disbelievers, and then the desired conclusion is obtained.
Source pages p. 380

Commentary
This passage presents a proof from the verse that a specific blazing fire is reserved for the most wretched who denied and turned away. Razi anticipates an objection: perhaps this verse refers only to a particular fire, not to all hellfires. He answers that all hellfires are necessarily blazing, and the verse indicates that the blazing fire afflicts the disbelievers. Thus, by extension, any fire that is blazing afflicts only disbelievers, so sinful believers who do not deny are excluded. The argument relies on the attribute 'blazing' being characteristic of all hellfires.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that the verse only speaks about a particular fire, so sinful believers could still enter other hellfires.
Correction: Razi shows that all hellfires are 'blazing,' and the verse uses that attribute, so the ruling applies universally.

Checkpoint
What attribute of hellfire does Razi use to generalize the verse?
A) It is eternal
B) It is blazing
C) It is painful
D) It is dark

Key Takeaway
Razi uses the attribute 'blazing' to show that the Quranic verse about a specific fire covers all hellfires, excluding sinful believers.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The verse describes the 'most wretched' as those who deny and turn away. When you read the Quran or hear reminders, do you ever catch yourself mentally rejecting or ignoring what is hard for you to accept? Is there an area of your life where you are 'turning away' rather than submitting? What will you do today to face it?
?
Razi's argument comforts believers that they are not destined for the blazing fire. But does this comfort make you complacent? Reflect: Is your faith alive? What signs in your life prove you are truly a believer, not just someone who hopes to be saved without effort? Ask Allah to strengthen your faith and save you from hypocrisy.
